# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Summary

I found and documented **32 key Java source files** across the kafka repository that implement SASL broker-side authentication:

### Key Components:

1. **Server Authenticator**: `SaslServerAuthenticator` - the central orchestrator of the authentication lifecycle
2. **Authentication Context**: `SaslAuthenticationContext` - encapsulates the authentication state
3. **SASL Mechanisms** (4 types):
   - **PLAIN**: `PlainSaslServer`, `PlainSaslServerProvider`, `PlainServerCallbackHandler`
   - **SCRAM**: `ScramSaslServer`, `ScramSaslServerProvider`, `ScramServerCallbackHandler`, `ScramMechanism`
   - **GSSAPI/Kerberos**: `KerberosLogin`, `KerberosName`, `KerberosRule`, `KerberosShortNamer`
   - **OAuthBearer**: `OAuthBearerSaslServer`, `OAuthBearerSaslServerProvider`

4. **Infrastructure**: JAAS context management, credential caching, callback handlers, and channel builders

The detailed findings have been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, key symbols, the authentication call chain, and a comprehensive narrative explaining how Kafka's broker-side SASL authentication works.

It handles the SASL handshake protocol, mechanism negotiation, and delegates to mechanism-specific SaslServer implementations. The createSaslServer() method selects the appropriate mechanism implementation based on the negotiated SASL mechanism.\\n\\n2. **Authentication Context Lifecycle**: SaslAuthenticationContext (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/SaslAuthenticationContext.java) encapsulates the authentication context during the authentication process, wrapping javax.security.sasl.SaslServer and providing security protocol, client address, and listener information.\\n\\n3. **PLAIN Mechanism**: The PLAIN mechanism is implemented through PlainSaslServer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainSaslServer.java), which implements the javax.security.sasl.SaslServer interface. The PlainSaslServerProvider (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainSaslServerProvider.java) registers the PlainSaslServerFactory that creates PLAIN server instances. PlainServerCallbackHandler (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainServerCallbackHandler.java) handles the JAAS callbacks for credential validation using the user_<username> format from JAAS configuration.\\n\\n4. **SCRAM Mechanism**: The SCRAM mechanism implementation includes ScramSaslServer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java) with ScramSaslServerProvider (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServerProvider.java) handling both SCRAM-SHA-256 and SCRAM-SHA-512 variants via ScramMechanism (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramMechanism.java). ScramServerCallbackHandler (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramServerCallbackHandler.java) manages credential and token validation using CredentialCache, while ScramFormatter (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramFormatter.java) handles SCRAM message formatting and credential generation.\\n\\n5. **GSSAPI/Kerberos Mechanism**: Kerberos authentication is handled through KerberosLogin (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosLogin.java) and KerberosClientCallbackHandler (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosClientCallbackHandler.java). Server-side GSSAPI uses Java's built-in GSSAPI provider. KerberosName (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosName.java) and KerberosShortNamer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosShortNamer.java) handle principal name mapping according to JAAS rules defined in KerberosRule (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosRule.java).\\n\\n6. **OAuthBearer Mechanism**: OAuthBearerSaslServer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/OAuthBearerSaslServer.java) implements OAuth 2.0 token-based authentication with OAuthBearerSaslServerProvider (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/OAuthBearerSaslServerProvider.java) registering the OAuthBearerSaslServerFactory.\\n\\n7. **Mechanism Selection Infrastructure**: SaslChannelBuilder (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SaslChannelBuilder.java) orchestrates the creation of server-side authentication components. It loads JAAS contexts for enabled mechanisms, creates appropriate callback handlers based on the mechanism type, and builds the authenticator. ChannelBuilders (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ChannelBuilders.java) provides factory methods for creating SASL channel builders for both client and server modes.\\n\\n8. **Callback Handler Infrastructure**: SaslServerCallbackHandler (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerCallbackHandler.java) provides default callback handling for all SASL mechanisms, while mechanism-specific handlers (PlainServerCallbackHandler, ScramServerCallbackHandler) override behavior for their respective mechanisms. AuthenticateCallbackHandler (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/AuthenticateCallbackHandler.java) is the interface that all callback handlers must implement.\\n\\n9. **JAAS Context Management**: JaasContext (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/JaasContext.java) and JaasConfig (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/JaasConfig.java) manage JAAS configuration loading and context creation for both static and dynamic JAAS configurations. LoginManager (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/LoginManager.java) manages the lifecycle of JAAS login modules.\\n\\n10. **Credential Storage**: CredentialCache (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/CredentialCache.java) provides in-memory caching of credentials for SCRAM mechanisms, supporting dynamic credential updates via broker admin operations.\\n\\nThe authentication flow begins when a client connects to a SASL listener. SaslChannelBuilder builds the server-side channel with appropriate JAAS contexts for all enabled mechanisms. SaslServerAuthenticator receives the initial SASL handshake request, extracts the client's preferred mechanism, creates a SaslServer instance via the appropriate mechanism provider, and proceeds with the SASL token exchange until authentication succeeds or fails. Throughout this process, the mechanism-specific SaslServer implementations handle the cryptographic and validation logic, with callback handlers bridging to the broker's credential stores and authorization rules.\"\n}\n",
